title="Portal:England">England&#32;portal</a>  <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">Other countries</a></li>\n<li><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_England" class="extiw" title="commons:Atlas of England">Atlas</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_England" title="Template:Politics of England"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_England" title="Template talk:Politics of England"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_England&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>North West England</b>, one of nine official <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_England" title="Regions of England">regions of England</a>, consists of the five <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">counties</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cheshire" title="Cheshire">Cheshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a>. The North West had a population of 7,052,000 in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Manchester_population_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manchester_population-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom_by_population" title="Countries of the United Kingdom by population">third-most populated region</a> in the United Kingdom after the <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Geographic features of the North West</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:144px;overflow:hidden"><a data-file-height="480" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_District" title="Lake District">Lake District</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:144px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:The_edge_of_Greenfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_26255.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/The_edge_of_Greenfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_26255.jpg/192px-The_edge_of_Greenfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_26255.jpg" width="192" height="144" District">Peak District</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:144px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Beeston_Walk_-_10th_April_2005_(16).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Beeston_Walk_-_10th_April_2005_%2816%29.JPG/192px-Beeston_Walk_-_10th_April_2005_%2816%29.JPG" width="192" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Beeston_Walk_-_10th_April_2005_%2816%29.JPG/288px-Beeston_Walk_-_10th_April_2005_%2816%29.JPG 1.5x, /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Cheshire_Plain" title="Cheshire Plain">Cheshire Plain</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:144px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Morecambe_Bay_from_Park_Point_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1236235.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Morecambe_Bay_from_Park_Point_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1236235.jpg/192px-Morecambe_Bay_from_Park_Point_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1236235.jpg" width="192" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Morecambe_Bay_from_Park_Point_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1236235.jpg/288px-Morecambe_Bay_from_Park_Point_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1236235.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Morecambe_Bay_from_Park_Point_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1236235.jpg/384px-Morecambe_Bay_from_Park_Point_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1236235.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Morecambe_Bay" title="Morecambe Bay">Morecambe Bay</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>North West England is bounded to the east by the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a> and to the west by the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a>. The region extends from the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Borders" title="Scottish Borders">Scottish Borders</a> in the north to the <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(region)" title="West Midlands (region)">West Midlands</a> region in the south. To its southwest is <a href="/wiki/North_Wales" title="North Wales">North Wales</a>. Amongst the better known of the North West\'s <a href="/wiki/Physiography" class="mw-redirect" title="Physiography">physiographical features</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Lake_District" title="Lake District">Lake District</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cheshire_Plain" title="Cheshire Plain">Cheshire Plain</a>. The highest point in North West England (and the highest peak in England) is <a href="/wiki/Scafell_Pike" title="Scafell Pike">Scafell Pike</a>, Cumbria, at a height of 3,209 feet (978&#160;m).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a> is the largest natural lake in England. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Broad_Crag_Tarn&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Broad Crag Tarn (page does not exist)">Broad Crag Tarn</a> on <a href="/wiki/Broad_Crag" title="Broad Crag">Broad Crag</a> is England\'s highest lake. <a href="/wiki/Wast_Water" title="Wast Water">Wast Water</a> is England\'s deepest lake, being <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lakedistrict.gov.uk/learning/factsandfigures">74m deep</a>.\n</p><p>A mix of rural and urban landscape, two large <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbations</a>, centred on <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, occupy much of the south of the region. The north of the region, comprising Cumbria and northern Lancashire, is largely rural, as is the far south which encompasses parts of the Cheshire Plain and Peak District.\n</p><p>The region includes parts of three <a href="/wiki/National_parks_of_England_and_Wales" title="National parks of England and Wales">National parks</a> (all of the <a href="/wiki/Lake_District" title="Lake District">Lake District</a>, and small parts of the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Dales" title="Yorkshire Dales">Yorkshire Dales</a>) and three areas of <a href="/wiki/Areas_of_Outstanding_Natural_Beauty" class="mw-redirect" title="Areas of Outstanding Natural Beauty">Areas of Outstanding Natural Beauty</a> (all of <a href="/wiki/Arnside_and_Silverdale" title="Arnside and Silverdale">Arnside and Silverdale</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Solway_Coast" title="Solway Coast">Solway Coast</a>, and almost all of the <a href="/wiki/Forest_of_Bowland" title="Forest of Bowland">Forest of Bowland</a>).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span (borough)">Rochdale</a>, <i>f</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/City_of_Salford" title="City of Salford">Salford</a>, <i>g</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Stockport" title="Stockport">Stockport</a>, <i>h</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tameside" title="Tameside">Tameside</a>, <i>i</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Trafford" title="Trafford">Trafford</a>, <i>j</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wigan_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" <i>f</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Wyre" title="Borough of Wyre">Wyre</a>, <i>g</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/City_of_Lancaster" title="City of Lancaster">Lancaster</a>, <i>h</i>)&#160;<a <i>l</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hyndburn" title="Hyndburn">Hyndburn</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">8.&#160;<a href="/wiki/Blackpool" title="Blackpool">Blackpool</a> U.A.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">9.&#160;<a href="/wiki/Blackburn_with_Darwen" title="Blackburn with Darwen">Blackburn with Darwen</a> U.A.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">10.&#160;<a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a>&#160;*</td>\n<td><i>a</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Knowsley" title="Metropolitan Borough of Knowsley">Knowsley</a>, <i>b</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, <i>c</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/St_Helens_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="St Helens (borough)">St. Helens</a>, <i>d</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Sefton" title="Metropolitan Borough of Sefton">Sefton</a>, <i>e</i>)&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wirral_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wirral (borough)">Wirral</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>*<a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_county" title="Metropolitan county">metropolitan county</a>\n</p><p>After abolition of the Greater Manchester and Merseyside County Councils in 1986, power was transferred to the Metropolitan Boroughs, effectively making them Unitary Authorities. In April 2011, Greater Manchester gained a top-tier administrative body in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Combined_Authority" title="Greater Manchester Combined Authority">Greater Manchester Combined Authority</a>, which means the 10 Greater Manchester Boroughs are once again second-tier authorities.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Population.2C_density_and_settlements"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Population,_density_and_settlements">Population, density and settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Population, density and settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Source: Office for National Statistics Mid Year Population Estimates<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Region/County\n</th>\n<th>Population\n</th>\n<th>Population Density\n</th>\n<th>Largest Manchester</a>\n</td>\n<td>2,629,400\n</td>\n<td>2,016/km\xc2\xb2\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> (510,700) (2012 est.)<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Urban_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Manchester Urban Area">Greater Manchester Urban Area</a> (2,240,230)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>\n</td>\n<td>1,449,600\n</td>\n<td>468/km\xc2\xb2\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Blackpool" title="Blackpool">Blackpool</a> (142,100)<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Preston,_Lancashire" title="Preston, Lancashire">Preston</a>/<a href="/wiki/Chorley" title="Chorley">Chorley</a>/<a href="/wiki/Leyland,_Lancashire" title="Leyland, Lancashire">Leyland</a> Urban Area (335,000)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Urban_Area" title="Liverpool Urban Area">Liverpool Urban Area</a> (816,000)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Cheshire" title="Cheshire">Cheshire</a>\n</td>\n<td>1,003,600\n</td>\n<td>424/km\xc2\xb2\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Warrington" title="Warrington">Warrington</a> (202,228)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Warrington" title="Warrington">Warrington</a> (202,228)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a>\n</td>\n<td>496,200\n</td>\n<td>73/km\xc2\xb2\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Cumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlisle, Cumbria">Carlisle</a> (71,773)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Cumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlisle, Cumbria">Carlisle</a> (71,773)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>North West England\'s population accounts for just over 13% of England\'s overall population. 37.86% of the North West\'s population resides in Greater Manchester, 21.39% in Lancashire, 20.30% in Merseyside, 14.76% in Cheshire and 7.41% live in the largest county by area, Cumbria.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_Arch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1021559.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Chinese_Arch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1021559.jpg/220px-Chinese_Arch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1021559.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Chinese_Arch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1021559.jpg/330px-Chinese_Arch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1021559.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Chinese_Arch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1021559.jpg/440px-Chinese_Arch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1021559.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="519" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_Arch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1021559.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Liverpool" title="Chinatown, Liverpool">Liverpool Chinatown</a> is the oldest Chinese community in Europe.</div></div></div>\n<p>According to 2009 <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a> estimates,<sup id="cite_ref-2009ethnicity_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009ethnicity-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> 91.6% (6,323,300) of people in the region describe themselves as \'White\': 88.4% (6,101,100) <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a>, 1.0% (67,200) <a href="/wiki/Irish_Briton" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Briton">White Irish</a> and 2.2% (155,000) <a href="/wiki/White_Other_(United_Kingdom_Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="White Other (United Kingdom Census)">White Other</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> hundreds of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh people</a> migrated to the North West of England to work in the coal mines. Parts with notably high populations with Welsh ancestry as a result of this include <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skelmersdale" title="Skelmersdale">Skelmersdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Widnes" title="Widnes">Widnes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halewood" title="Halewood">Halewood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wallasey" title="Wallasey">Wallasey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashton-in-Makerfield" title="Ashton-in-Makerfield">Ashton-in-Makerfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Birkenhead" title="Birkenhead">Birkenhead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Mixed" class="mw-redirect" title="British Mixed">Mixed Race</a> population makes up 1.3% (93,800) of the region\'s population. There are 323,800 <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">South Asians</a>, making up 4.7% of the population, and 1.1% <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black Britons</a> (80,600). 0.6% of the population (39,900) are <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">Chinese</a> and 0.5% (36,500) of people belong to another ethnic group.\n</p><p>North West England is a very diverse region, with Manchester and Liverpool amongst the most diverse cities in Europe. 19.4% of <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_with_Darwen" title="Blackburn with Darwen">Blackburn with Darwen</a>\'s population are Muslim, the third-highest among all local authorities in the United Kingdom and the highest outside London. Areas such as <a href="/wiki/Moss_Side" title="Moss Side">Moss Side</a> in Greater Manchester are home to a 30%+ <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black British</a> population. In contrast, the town of St. Helens in Merseyside, unusually for a city area, has a very low percentage of ethnic minorities with 98% identifying as White British.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The City of Liverpool, over 800 years old, is one of the few places in Britain where ethnic minority populations can be traced back over dozens of generations: being the closest major city in England to Ireland, it is home to a significant ethnic Irish population, with the city being home to one of the first ever <a href="/wiki/British_African-Caribbean_people" title="British African-Caribbean people">Afro-Caribbean</a> communities in the UK, as well as the oldest Chinatown in Europe.\n</p><p><b>Summarised</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li>There are around 400,000 people living in the North West of any Asian ethnicity</li>\n<li>Around 125,000 people from the North West are of full or partial Sub-African and/or Caribbean descent</li>\n<li>The single largest non-white ethnic group in the North West are Pakistanis, numbering at least 144,400</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Place_of_birth">Place of birth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Place of birth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The list below is not how many people belong to each ethnic group (e.g. there are over 25,000 ethnic <a href="/wiki/Italians_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Italians in the United Kingdom">Italians</a> in Manchester alone,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> whilst only 6,000 Italian-born people live in the North West). The fifteen most common countries of birth in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">2001</a> for North West citizens were as follows (2008 estimates, where available, in brackets)<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2008_estimates_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2008_estimates-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jodrell_Bank_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Jodrell_Bank_%281%29.jpg/220px-Jodrell_Bank_%281%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Jodrell_Bank_%281%29.jpg/330px-Jodrell_Bank_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Jodrell_Bank_%281%29.jpg/440px-Jodrell_Bank_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jodrell_Bank_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Jodrell_Bank_Observatory" title="Jodrell Bank Observatory">Jodrell Bank</a> <a href="/wiki/Lovell_Telescope" title="Lovell Telescope">Lovell</a> 76-m <a href="/wiki/Radio_telescope" title="Radio telescope">radio telescope</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Withington" title="Lower Withington">Lower Withington</a>, built in August 1957, is the world\'s third largest steerable telescope, and was the largest until 1971. It was designed by Sheffield\'s Sir <a href="/wiki/Charles_Husband" title="Charles Husband">Charles Husband</a> and built of steel from <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe" title="Scunthorpe">Scunthorpe</a></div></div></div>\n<ul><li>England \xe2\x80\x93 6,169,753</li>\n<li>Scotland \xe2\x80\x93 109,163</li>\n<li>Wales \xe2\x80\x93 73,850</li>\n<li>Ireland \xe2\x80\x93 56,887 (51,000 in 2008)</li>\n<li>Pakistan \xe2\x80\x93 46,529 (58,000 in 2008)</li>\n<li>Northern Ireland \xe2\x80\x93 34,879</li>\n<li>India \xe2\x80\x93 34,600 (48,000 in 2008)</li>\n<li>Germany \xe2\x80\x93 19,931 (25,000 in 2008)</li>\n<li>China and Hong Kong \xe2\x80\x93 15,491</li>\n<li>Bangladesh \xe2\x80\x93 13,746</li>\n<li>South Africa \xe2\x80\x93 7,740</li>\n<li>United States \xe2\x80\x93 7,037</li>\n<li>Jamaica \xe2\x80\x93 6,661</li>\n<li>Italy \xe2\x80\x93 6,325</li>\n<li>Australia \xe2\x80\x93 5,880</li>\n<li>Poland \xe2\x80\x93 (37,000 in 2008)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The table below is based on the <a href="/wiki/2011_UK_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 UK Census">2011 UK Census</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Region\n</th>\n<th>Christian\n</th>\n<th>Muslim\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Hindu" England\n</td>\n<td>67.3%\n</td>\n<td>5.1%\n</td>\n<td>0.5%\n</td>\n<td>0.1%\n</td>\n<td>0.4%\n</td>\n<td>0.3%\n</td>\n<td>0.3%\n</td>\n<td>26.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>England\n</td>\n<td>59.4%\n</td>\n<td>5.0%\n</td>\n<td>1.5%\n</td>\n<td>0.8%\n</td>\n<td>0.5%\n</td>\n<td>0.5%\n</td>\n<td>0.4%\n</td>\n<td>31.9%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>One in five of the population in the North West is <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> a result of large-scale <a href="/wiki/Irish_migration_to_Great_Britain" title="Irish migration to Great Britain">Irish emigration</a> in the nineteenth century<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> as well as the high number of English <a href="/wiki/Recusancy" title="Recusancy">recusants</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teenage_pregnancy">Teenage pregnancy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Teenage pregnancy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For top-tier authorities, Manchester has the highest <a href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Teenage pregnancy in the United Kingdom">teenage pregnancy</a> rate in the region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> For council districts, <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Burnley" title="Borough of Burnley">Burnley</a> has the highest rate, closely followed by <a href="/wiki/Hyndburn" title="Hyndburn">Hyndburn</a>, both in Lancashire.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_deprivation">Social deprivation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Social deprivation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Of the nine regions of the England, the North West has the <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom_by_GVA_per_capita" title="Countries of the United Kingdom by GVA per capita">fourth-highest GVA per capita</a>\xe2\x80\x94the highest outside southern England. Despite this the region has above average <a href="/wiki/Multiple_deprivation_index" title="Multiple deprivation index">multiple deprivation</a> with wealth heavily concentrated on very affluent areas like rural Cheshire, rural Lancashire, and south Cumbria. As measured by the <a href="/wiki/Indices_of_deprivation_2007" title="Indices of deprivation 2007">Indices of deprivation 2007</a>, the region has many more <a href="/wiki/ONS_coding_system" title="ONS coding system">Lower Layer Super Output Areas</a> in the 20% most deprived districts than the 20% least deprived council districts.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Only <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East England</a> shows more indicators of deprivation than the North West, but the number of affluent areas in the North West is very similar to <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a>.\n</p><p>The most deprived local authority areas in the region (based on specific wards within those borough areas) are, in descending order\xe2\x80\x94Liverpool, Manchester, Knowsley, Blackpool, Salford, Blackburn with Darwen, Burnley, Rochdale, Barrow-in-Furness, Halton, Hyndburn, Oldham, Pendle, St Helens, Preston, Bolton, Tameside, Wirral, Wigan, Copeland, Sefton, and Rossendale. These areas almost exclusively have Labour MPs, with the sole exception of Lib Dem John Pugh in <a href="/wiki/Southport_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Southport (UK Parliament constituency)">Sefton</a>. <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Burnley" title="Borough of Burnley">Burnley</a> is the only of these not to have a Labour council.\n</p><p>In 2007 when Cheshire still had district councils, the least deprived council districts in the region by council district, in descending order, were\xe2\x80\x94Congleton, Ribble Valley, Macclesfield, and South Lakeland.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> These areas have Conservative MPs, except South Lakeland has a Lib Dem and Labour MPs. At county level, before it was split into two, Cheshire was the least deprived, followed by Trafford, and by Warrington and Stockport.\n</p><p>In March 2011, the overall <a href="/wiki/Jobseeker%27s_Allowance" title="Jobseeker&#39;s Allowance">unemployment claimant</a> count was 4.2% for the region. Inside the region the highest was Liverpool with 6.8%, followed by Knowsley on 6.3%, Halton with 5.5% and Rochdale with 5.1%. The lowest claimant count is in <a href="/wiki/Eden_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eden (district)">Eden</a> (Cumbria) and <a href="/wiki/Ribble_Valley" title="Ribble Valley">Ribble Valley</a> (Lancashire) each with 1.3%, followed by <a href="/wiki/South_Lakeland" title="South Lakeland">South Lakeland</a> with 1.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_(North_West_England).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28North_West_England%29.svg/220px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28North_West_England%29.svg.png" width="220" height="475" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28North_West_England%29.svg/330px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28North_West_England%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28North_West_England%29.svg/440px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28North_West_England%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="713" data-file-height="1540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_(North_West_England).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General election results in 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>, the area was dominated by the Labour Party. Forty-five percent of the region\'s electorate voted Labour, 31% Conservative, 14% UKIP, 6% Liberal Democrat and 3% Greens; however, by number of parliamentary seats, Labour have 50, the Conservatives have 23, and the Liberal Democrats have 2. The Lib Dems\' North West seats are in Southport and south Cumbria; Labour dominates Greater Manchester, and the Conservatives\' vote is concentrated in affluent suburban areas such as <a href="/wiki/Cheadle_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cheadle (UK Parliament constituency)">Cheadle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hazel_Grove_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Hazel Grove (UK Parliament constituency)">Hazel Grove</a> and <a href="/wiki/Altrincham_and_Sale_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Altrincham and Sale West (UK Parliament constituency)">Altrincham and Sale West</a>. Labour seats also predominate in Merseyside. Cheshire is mostly Conservative, and Lancashire is competitive between Labour and Conservative (8 seats each); the Labour seats in Lancashire are concentrated in the south of the county along the <a href="/wiki/M65_motorway" title="M65 motorway">M65</a>. For the region, the Conservatives gained 3 seats; there was a 2.8% swing from Conservative to Labour.\n</p><p>In the 2010 general election, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Walton_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Liverpool Walton (UK Parliament constituency)">Liverpool Walton</a> was the safest seat in the UK, with a 57% majority, and in 2015 this was repeated with a 72% majority for <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rotheram" title="Steve Rotheram">Steve Rotheram</a> (Labour), when an astonishing 81% of the electorate voted for him (UKIP came second with 9%). In the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Central_by-election,_2012" title="Manchester Central by-election, 2012">by-election of 2012</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Manchester Central (UK Parliament constituency)">Manchester Central</a> has the record for the lowest turnout in the UK\xe2\x80\x9418%. <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Dunwoody" title="Gwyneth Dunwoody">Gwyneth Dunwoody</a>, for Crewe and Nantwich, was the longest serving female MP until her death in 2008.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2009 (United Kingdom)">2009 European Election</a>, 26% voted Conservative, 20% Labour, 16% UKIP and 14.3% Liberal Democrat.\n</p>\n<div role="navigation" Independence Party">UKIP</a> (2)</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_and_dialect">Language and dialect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Language and dialect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The earliest known language spoken in the North West was a dialect of the <a href="/wiki/Common_Brittonic" title="Common Brittonic">Brythonic language</a> spoken across much of Britain from at least the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> up to the arrival of English in the first millennium AD. Fragments of this early language are seen in the inscriptions and place names of the Roman era. In some parts of the region, the Brythonic dialect developed into the medieval language known today as <a href="/wiki/Cumbric" title="Cumbric">Cumbric</a>, which continued to be spoken perhaps as late as the 12th century in the north of Cumbria. This early Celtic heritage remains today in place names such as <a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Cumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlisle, Cumbria">Carlisle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penrith,_Cumbria" title="Penrith, Cumbria">Penrith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eccles,_Greater_Manchester" title="Eccles, Greater Manchester">Eccles</a>, and many river names such as <a href="/wiki/River_Cocker,_Cumbria" title="River Cocker, Cumbria">Cocker</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Kent" title="River Kent">Kent</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Eden,_Cumbria" title="River Eden, Cumbria">Eden</a>.\n</p><p>English may have been spoken in the North West from around the 7th century AD, when the Anglo-Saxon kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Northumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Northumbria">Northumbria</a> first appears to have made inroads west of the Pennines. The language at this time would have been the Northumbrian dialect of <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a>. The high percentage of English place names in the region as a whole suggests English became almost ubiquitous over the coming centuries, particularly in the area south of the Lake District. Manchester, Liverpool, Lancaster, Blackburn and Preston are among the region\'s many English place names. In the 9th to the 11th centuries, Danes from the east and Norsemen from Ireland and Scotland began settling in the area. The North West is really the only area of England where Norse settlement was significant and their influence remains in the place names and dialect of the region. Elements like <i>fell</i>, <i>thwaite</i> and <i>tarn</i>, which are particularly common in Cumbria, are all Norse. The numerous Kirkbys and place names with \'holm\' and \'dale\' show the <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavian</a> influence throughout the North West.\n</p><p>Through the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> the dialects of the North West would have been considerably different from those spoken in the Midlands and south. It was only with the spread of literacy (particularly with the publication of the <a href="/wiki/King_James_Version" title="King James Version">King James Bible</a>) that <a href="/wiki/Standard_English" title="Standard English">Standard English</a> spread to the region. Even so, local dialects continued to be used and were relatively widespread until the 19th and 20th centuries.\n</p><p>In modern times, English is the most spoken language in the North West, with a large percentage of the population fluent in it, and close to 100% conversational in it. To the north-east of the region, within the historic boundaries of <a href="/wiki/Cumberland" title="Cumberland">Cumberland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cumbrian_dialect" title="Cumbrian dialect">Cumbrian dialect</a> is dominant. The historical county of <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a> covered a vast amount of land, and the <a href="/wiki/Lancashire_dialect" title="Lancashire dialect">Lancashire dialect</a> and accent is still predominant throughout the county, and stretches as far north as <a href="/wiki/Furness" title="Furness">Furness</a> in South Cumbria to parts of north <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a> in the south of the region. The region boasts some of the most distinctive accents in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Scouse" title="Scouse">Scouse</a> accent, which originates from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and its surrounding areas, and the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_dialect" title="Manchester dialect">Manc</a> accent, deriving from the central <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> district. The region\'s accents are among those referred to as \'<a href="/wiki/English_language_in_Northern_England" title="English language in Northern England">Northern English</a>\'.\n</p><p>Large immigrant populations in the North West result in the presence of significant immigrant languages. South Asian languages such as <a href="/wiki/Urdu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> are widespread,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> with the largest amount of speakers residing in <a href="/wiki/Preston,_Lancashire" title="Preston, Lancashire">Preston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackburn" title="Blackburn">Blackburn</a> and Manchester. The <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">Chinese</a> once made up the largest minority in the region (as Liverpool has one of the oldest Chinese settlements in Europe), and still do to the far north where Chinese is spoken by small but significant communities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Since the enlargement of the EU, over one million <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> have immigrated to the UK, a large number of them settling in the North West.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Places such as <a href="/wiki/Crewe" title="Crewe">Crewe</a> as well as larger cities make <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> written information available for the public, to much controversy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Other immigrant languages with a presence in the North West are Spanish, mainly amongst the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Briton" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin American Briton">Latin American</a> communities in <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> as well as various other Eastern European and Asian languages.\n</p><p>The most taught languages in schools across the North West are English, French and German. Spanish and Italian are available at more senior levels and, in cities such as Manchester and Liverpool, even Urdu and Mandarin are being taught to help maintain links between the local minority populations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eurostat_NUTS">Eurostat NUTS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Eurostat NUTS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics</a> (NUTS), North West is a level-1 NUTS region, coded "UKD", which (since 2015) is subdivided as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table title="Darwen">Darwen</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hindley,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hindley, Greater Manchester">Hindley</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cheadle_Hulme" title="Cheadle Hulme">Cheadle Hulme</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fleetwood" title="Fleetwood">Fleetwood</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Congleton" title="Congleton">Congleton</a>, CH</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swinton,_Greater_Manchester" title="Swinton, Greater Manchester">Swinton</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Workington" title="Workington">Workington</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_Turton" title="South Turton">South Turton</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Westhoughton" title="Westhoughton">Westhoughton</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wilmslow" title="Wilmslow">Wilmslow</a>, CH</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ormskirk" title="Ormskirk">Ormskirk</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Golborne" title="Golborne">Golborne</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Whitehaven" title="Whitehaven">Whitehaven</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stalybridge" title="Stalybridge">Stalybridge</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marple,_Greater_Manchester" title="Marple, Greater Manchester">Marple</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Whitefield,_Greater_Manchester" title="Whitefield, Greater Manchester">Whitefield</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Droylsden" title="Droylsden">Droylsden</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Penwortham" title="Penwortham">Penwortham</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Formby" title="Formby">Formby</a>, ME</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Litherland" title="Litherland">Litherland</a>, ME</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Newton-le-Willows" title="Newton-le-Willows">Newton-le-Willows</a>, ME</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Atherton,_Greater_Manchester" title="Atherton, Greater Manchester">Atherton</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rawtenstall" title="Rawtenstall">Rawtenstall</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Royton" title="Royton">Royton</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Walkden" title="Walkden">Walkden</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Shaw_and_Crompton" title="Shaw and Crompton">Shaw and Crompton</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Failsworth" title="Failsworth">Failsworth</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maghull" title="Maghull">Maghull</a>, ME</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Halewood" title="Halewood">Halewood</a>, ME</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Horwich" title="Horwich">Horwich</a>, GM</li></ul>\n<p><b>Population &gt; 10,000</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Irlam" title="Irlam">Irlam</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dukinfield" title="Dukinfield">Dukinfield</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Colne" title="Colne">Colne</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Poulton-le-Fylde" title="Poulton-le-Fylde">Poulton-le-Fylde</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sandbach" title="Sandbach">Sandbach</a>, CH</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ramsbottom" title="Ramsbottom">Ramsbottom</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Moreton,_Merseyside" title="Moreton, Merseyside">Moreton</a>, ME</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bramhall" title="Bramhall">Bramhall</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nantwich" title="Nantwich">Nantwich</a>, CH</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Haslingden" title="Haslingden">Haslingden</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Upton,_Merseyside" title="Upton, Merseyside">Upton</a>, ME</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hazel_Grove" title="Hazel Grove">Hazel Grove</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Clitheroe" title="Clitheroe">Clitheroe</a>, LA</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Neston" title="Neston">Neston</a>, CH</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tyldesley" title="Tyldesley">Tyldesley</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Romiley" title="Romiley">Romiley</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pendlebury" title="Pendlebury">Pendlebury</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Woodley,_Greater_Manchester" title="Woodley, Greater Manchester">Woodley</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ulverston" title="Ulverston">Ulverston</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Penrith,_Cumbria" title="Penrith, Cumbria">Penrith</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maryport" title="Maryport">Maryport</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Heysham" title="Heysham">Heysham</a>, LA</li></ul>\n<p><b>Population &gt; 5,000</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frodsham" title="Frodsham">Frodsham</a>, CH</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gatley" title="Gatley">Gatley</a>, GM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dalton-in-Furness" title="Dalton-in-Furness">Dalton-in-Furness</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Windermere,_Cumbria_(town)" title="Windermere, Cumbria (town)">Windermere</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Millom" title="Millom">Millom</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cleator_Moor" title="Cleator Moor">Cleator Moor</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cockermouth" title="Cockermouth">Cockermouth</a>, CU</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carnforth" title="Carnforth">Carnforth</a>, LA</li></ul>\n</div>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_areas">Metropolitan areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Metropolitan areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of metropolitan areas in the United Kingdom">List of metropolitan areas in the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<p>The five largest metropolitan areas in the North West are as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Greater Manchester metropolitan area \xe2\x80\x93 2,556,000<sup id="cite_ref-j_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Liverpool/Birkenhead metropolitan area \xe2\x80\x93 2,241,000<sup id="cite_ref-j_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Blackburn" title="Blackburn">Blackburn</a>/<a href="/wiki/Burnley" title="Burnley">Burnley</a> \xe2\x80\x93 391,000<sup id="cite_ref-j_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Preston,_Lancashire" title="Preston, Lancashire">Preston</a> \xe2\x80\x93 354,000<sup id="cite_ref-j_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Blackpool" title="Blackpool">Blackpool</a> \xe2\x88\x92304,000<sup id="cite_ref-j_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Liverpool and Manchester are sometimes considered parts of a single large polynuclear <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis" title="Megalopolis">megalopolis</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> but are usually treated as separate metropolitan areas.<sup id="cite_ref-j_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In some studies, part of <a href="/wiki/Wigan" title="Wigan">Wigan</a> in Greater Manchester is considered part of the Liverpool metropolitan area.<sup id="cite_ref-j_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Elected_regional_assembly">Elected regional assembly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Elected regional assembly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_North_West_England.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Flag_of_North_West_England.svg/200px-Flag_of_North_West_England.svg.png" width="200" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Flag_of_North_West_England.svg/300px-Flag_of_North_West_England.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Flag_of_North_West_England.svg/400px-Flag_of_North_West_England.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_North_West_England.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_North_West_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag of North West England">Proposed flag for the region</a> designed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Saville_(artist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter Saville (artist)">Peter Saville</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>It is one of the two regions (along with <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a>) that were expected to hold a referendum on the establishment of an elected <a href="/wiki/Regional_assembly_(England)" title="Regional assembly (England)">regional assembly</a>. However, when the <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East</a> region of England rejected having an elected regional assembly in a referendum, further referendums were cancelled and the proposals for elected regional assemblies in England put on hold. The regional leaders\' forum, <a href="/wiki/North_West_Regional_Leaders_Board" title="North West Regional Leaders Board">4NW</a>, an unelected <a href="/wiki/Quango" title="Quango">quango</a>, is based on Waterside Drive in <a href="/wiki/Wigan" title="Wigan">Wigan</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament">European Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: European Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/North_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="North West England (European Parliament constituency)">North West England European Parliament constituency</a> has the same boundaries as the Region.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cumbria" title="History of Cumbria">History of Cumbria</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Lancashire" title="History of Lancashire">History of Lancashire</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Manchester" title="History of Manchester">History of Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Liverpool" title="History of Liverpool">History of Liverpool</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cheshire" title="History of Cheshire">History of Cheshire</a></div>\n<p>Ten English regions were established by the government in 1994. At that time, <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a>, which already had its own Government Office, formerly the Merseyside Task Force, was regarded as a separate region. In 1998, Merseyside was merged into the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080513064247/http://www.gonw.gov.uk/gonw/">North West region</a>. This action was controversial in some quarters.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Regional Government Offices were abolished in April 2011 by the Coalition Government.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_heritage">Scientific heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Scientific heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_engineering_in_Manchester" title="Science and engineering in Manchester">Science and engineering in Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_innovations_and_discoveries" title="List of British innovations and discoveries">List of British innovations and discoveries</a></div>\n<p>Sir <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Marsden" title="Ernest Marsden">Ernest Marsden</a> (of Blackburn) and <a href="/wiki/Hans_Geiger" title="Hans Geiger">Hans Geiger</a> conducted the <a href="/wiki/Geiger%E2%80%93Marsden_experiment" title="Geiger\xe2\x80\x93Marsden experiment">Geiger\xe2\x80\x93Marsden experiment</a> at the University of Manchester in 1909, where the <a href="/wiki/Geiger_counter" title="Geiger counter">Geiger counter</a> was invented, which demonstrated the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_nucleus" title="Atomic nucleus">atomic nucleus</a>. Sir <a href="/wiki/J._J._Thomson" title="J. J. Thomson">J. J. Thomson</a> of Cheetham Hill discovered the electron (given its name in 1891 by <a href="/wiki/George_Johnstone_Stoney" title="George Johnstone Stoney">George Johnstone Stoney</a>) in April 1897 and received the Nobel Prize for Physics in 1906; his son <a href="/wiki/George_Paget_Thomson" title="George Paget Thomson">George Paget Thomson</a> would win the Nobel Prize for Physics 1937 for discovering <a href="/wiki/Electron_diffraction" title="Electron diffraction">electron diffraction</a> (at the University of Aberdeen). <a href="/wiki/John_Dalton" title="John Dalton">John Dalton</a>, from Cumbria and moved to Manchester, developed <a href="/wiki/Atomic_theory" title="Atomic theory">atomic theory</a>. <a href="/wiki/William_Sturgeon" title="William Sturgeon">William Sturgeon</a> of Lancashire invented the <a href="/wiki/Electromagnet" title="Electromagnet">electromagnet</a> in 1825.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sydney_Chapman_(mathematician)" title="Sydney Chapman (mathematician)">Sydney Chapman</a>, a mathematician from <a href="/wiki/Eccles,_Greater_Manchester" title="Eccles, Greater Manchester">Eccles</a>, in 1930 explained the <a href="/wiki/Ozone%E2%80%93oxygen_cycle" title="Ozone\xe2\x80\x93oxygen cycle">ozone\xe2\x80\x93oxygen cycle</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Stratosphere" title="Stratosphere">stratosphere</a>, being the first to propose that atmospheric oxygen or ozone molecules absorb (harmful UVB and UVC) <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">ultraviolet</a> wavelengths of light in <a href="/wiki/Photodissociation" title="Photodissociation">photolysis</a>, to produce reactive single atoms which accumulate to form the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">ozone layer</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Graphene" title="Graphene">Graphene</a> was discovered at the University of Manchester in 2004 under Prof Sir <a href="/wiki/Andre_Geim" title="Andre Geim">Andre Geim</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Novoselov" title="Konstantin Novoselov">Konstantin Novoselov</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fluothane_packaging_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Fluothane_packaging_01.jpg/160px-Fluothane_packaging_01.jpg" width="160" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Fluothane_packaging_01.jpg/240px-Fluothane_packaging_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Fluothane_packaging_01.jpg/320px-Fluothane_packaging_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2030" data-file-height="4130" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fluothane_packaging_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Exhibit of ICI\'s Fluothane (Halothane), discovered at Widnes, at <a href="/wiki/Catalyst_Science_Discovery_Centre" title="Catalyst Science Discovery Centre">Catalyst Science Discovery Centre</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Spike_Island_(Cheshire)" title="Spike Island (Cheshire)">Spike Island</a> in Widnes</div></div></div>\n<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Calico_Printers%27_Association" title="Calico Printers&#39; Association">Calico Printers\' Association</a> in Manchester in 1941, <a href="/wiki/John_Rex_Whinfield" title="John Rex Whinfield">John Rex Whinfield</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=James_Tennant_Dickson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James Tennant Dickson (page does not exist)">James Tennant Dickson</a> discovered <a href="/wiki/Polyethylene_terephthalate" title="Polyethylene terephthalate">polyethylene terephthalate</a>, known as PET, a common <a href="/wiki/Polyester" title="Polyester">polyester</a> compound found in <a href="/wiki/Plastic_bottle" title="Plastic bottle">plastic bottles</a> and food, and also known as Terylene or Dacron. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheslene_and_Crepes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cheslene and Crepes (page does not exist)">Cheslene and Crepes</a> of Macclesfield discovered <a href="/wiki/Crimplene" title="Crimplene">crimplene</a> (the fabric that is now referred to as polyester). <a href="/w/index.php?title=ICI_Dyestuffs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ICI Dyestuffs (page does not exist)">ICI Dyestuffs</a> at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hexagon_House_(Manchester)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hexagon House (Manchester) (page does not exist)">Hexagon House</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Blackley" title="Blackley">Blackley</a> in north Manchester, discovered <a href="/wiki/Procion" title="Procion">Procion</a> dyes. At the <a href="/wiki/Winnington_Laboratory" title="Winnington Laboratory">Winnington Laboratory</a> on 27 March 1933, Eric Fawcett and Reginald Gibson discovered <a href="/wiki/Polyethylene" title="Polyethylene">polythene</a> in an ICI laboratory in Northwich, when reacting <a href="/wiki/Benzaldehyde" title="Benzaldehyde">benzaldehyde</a> with <a href="/wiki/Ethylene" title="Ethylene">ethene</a> at a pressure of 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_(unit)" title="Atmosphere (unit)">atmospheres</a>; the process was improved in 1935 by Sir <a href="/wiki/Michael_Perrin" title="Michael Perrin">Michael Perrin</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Halothane" title="Halothane">Halothane</a>, the world\'s first synthetic inhalation <a href="/wiki/General_anaesthetic" title="General anaesthetic">general anaesthetic</a> gas, was discovered in 1951 at ICI\'s <a href="/w/index.php?title=Widnes_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Widnes Laboratory (page does not exist)">Widnes Laboratory</a> by Wallasey\'s <a href="/wiki/Charles_Suckling" title="Charles Suckling">Charles Suckling</a>, and first tested on a patient in Manchester in 1956; it works by binding to the <a href="/wiki/GABA_receptor" title="GABA receptor">GABA receptor</a>. Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Charnley" title="John Charnley">John Charnley</a> of Bury invented the <a href="/wiki/Hip_replacement" title="Hip replacement">hip replacement</a> in 1962 at <a href="/wiki/Wrightington" title="Wrightington">Wrightington</a>, Lancashire, north-west of Wigan. <a href="/wiki/Clatterbridge_Hospital" title="Clatterbridge Hospital">Clatterbridge Hospital</a> in Bebington has a <a href="/wiki/Cyclotron" title="Cyclotron">cyclotron</a> (<a href="/wiki/Linear_particle_accelerator" title="Linear particle accelerator">linear accelerator</a>), and is the only hospital in the UK to offer <a href="/wiki/Proton_therapy" title="Proton therapy">proton therapy</a>.\n</p><p>Alderley Park opened in October 1957, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=ICI_Pharmaceuticals&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ICI Pharmaceuticals (page does not exist)">ICI Pharmaceuticals</a> was formed in the same year. In 1962 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dora_Richardson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dora Richardson (page does not exist)">Dora Richardson</a> of ICI discovered <a href="/wiki/Tamoxifen" title="Tamoxifen">tamoxifen</a>. ICI <a href="/wiki/Alderley_Park" title="Alderley Park">Alderley Park</a> later discovered <a href="/wiki/Anastrozole" title="Anastrozole">Anastrozole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fulvestrant" title="Fulvestrant">Fulvestrant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goserelin" title="Goserelin">Goserelin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bicalutamide" title="Bicalutamide">Bicalutamide</a>, later made by <a href="/wiki/Zeneca" title="Zeneca">Zeneca</a>. Sir James Black discovered <a href="/wiki/Beta_blocker" title="Beta blocker">beta blockers</a>\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Propranolol" title="Propranolol">propranolol</a> (Inderal) at Alderley Park in 1962. The <a href="/wiki/Wellcome_Trust" title="Wellcome Trust">Wellcome Foundation</a>, a provider of much of Britain\'s medical research, was based from 1966 to 1997 at <a href="/wiki/Crewe_Hall" title="Crewe Hall">Crewe Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Crewe_Green" title="Crewe Green">Crewe Green</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Clifford_Cocks" title="Clifford Cocks">Clifford Cocks</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_H._Ellis" title="James H. Ellis">James H. Ellis</a> from Cheshire, with <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_J._Williamson" title="Malcolm J. Williamson">Malcolm J. Williamson</a>, invented the <a href="/wiki/RSA_(cryptosystem)" title="RSA (cryptosystem)">RSA (algorithm)</a> in 1973 at GCHQ, used for <a href="/wiki/Public-key_cryptography" title="Public-key cryptography">public-key cryptography</a>. Sir <a href="/wiki/Richard_Owen" title="Richard Owen">Richard Owen</a> from Lancaster coined the word <i><a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaur</a></i> in 1842, and he founded the <a href="/wiki/Natural_History_Museum,_London" title="Natural History Museum, London">Natural History Museum, London</a>, opening in 1881.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_heritage">Industrial heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Industrial heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rainhill_Bridge,_from_Bury%27s_Liverpool_and_Manchester_Railway,_1831_-_artfinder_3408.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Rainhill_Bridge%2C_from_Bury%27s_Liverpool_and_Manchester_Railway%2C_1831_-_artfinder_3408.jpg/200px-Rainhill_Bridge%2C_from_Bury%27s_Liverpool_and_Manchester_Railway%2C_1831_-_artfinder_3408.jpg" width="200" height="160" class="thumbimage"
